Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnea is caused by an upper airway obstruction during sleep.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst are types of jaw tumors; they may cause swelling and airway obstruction, but this is very rare.
  Orbital fracture is a fracture of the bony socket which houses the eyeball and does not cause sleep apnea.
  TMJ ankylosis is the inability to open the jaw because of bony or fibrous adhesion in the jaw joint; it may also cause airway obstruction, but bilateral TMJ ankylosis is again a rare condition.
  Therefore, the closest option to the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Obstructive sleep apnoea is caused by the blockages in the upper airway during sleeping hours.
  Mandibular ameloblastoma and Dentigerous cysts affect the jaw and teeth respectively.
  Orbital fracture happens to the bones around the eye.
  Bilateral TMJ Ankylosis leads to limited movement in the jaw.
  None of these conditions are directly related to the blockages in the upper airway.
  Therefore, none of the above.
Action: Answer('None of the above')
Response 2:
Thought:
Obstructive sleep apnea is a condition in which breathing is interrupted while sleeping.
It is caused by the relaxation of the muscles in the throat and tongue.
Mandibular ameloblastoma and dentigerous cyst are dental problems that may require surgery but are not related to obstructive sleep apnea.
Orbital fracture is a type of facial fracture that affects the eye socket and may cause double vision or difficulty moving the eye, but it does not cause obstructive sleep apnea.
Bilateral TMJ (temporomandibular joint) ankylosis is a condition in which there is a fusion of the jaw bone to the skull bone, which can cause difficulty with eating and speaking.
Obstructive sleep apnea can be caused by TMJ disorders, as they can cause the tongue to fall back and block the airway during sleep.
Therefore, the most likely answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  Upon obstruction of the airway, the muscles around the airway relax and collapse creating breathing trouble leading to Obstructive Sleep Apnea (OSA).
  Mandibular Ameloblastoma and Dentigerous Cyst mainly occur in the lower jaw. Although it may lead to airway obstruction, it is not common.
  Orbital fracture is an injury to the eye socket which won't cause airway obstruction.
  Bilateral TMJ (Temporomandibular Joint) ankylosis is fusion of the jaw bone to skull bone, which can cause airway obstruction in rare cases.
  Therefore, the more likely cause for Obstructive Sleep Apnea is Bilateral TMJ ankylosis. 
Answer: Answer("D")

  Dentigerous cyst is a fluid-filled sac that forms around an unerupted tooth, unlikely to cause a blockage of the airway.
  Orbital fracture affects the bones around the eye and is unlikely to cause a blockage of the airway.
  TMJ (temporomandibular joint) is closely related to breathing and is a possible cause of airway obstruction.
  Bilateral TMJ ankylosis can cause difficulty in opening the mouth; it can cause airway obstruction and therefore obstructive sleep apnoea.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis.

Topic: Dental
Question: Gum pads are divided into following segments:
Choices:
  A: 3 in each quadrant
  B: 2 in each jaw
  C: 5 in each quadrant
  D: 2 in each quadrant
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Gum pads are placed on the teeth to isolate them during dental procedures.
  Each quadrant of the mouth typically has 8 teeth.
  2 or 3 gum pads are usually placed in each quadrant to isolate the teeth being worked on.
  Answer A and C is too many gum pads for each quadrant.
  Answer B is too few gum pads for each quadrant. 
  Therefore, the most likely answer is D, 2 in each quadrant.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Gum pads are positioned between teeth where flossing cannot reach.
  The number of gum pads varies based on their position in the mouth.
  Jaw is not used to divide the gum pads.
  Three seems to be a large number per quadrant and two seems too less.
  Five is also not likely since it's too high.
  Two pads per quadrant seems appropriate.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Gum pads are used to treat gum disease.
  The dentist or dental hygienist places a small pad on the gum tissue.
  Gum pads are placed in the specific areas of the mouth that require treatment.
  A quadrant refers to one-quarter of the mouth.
  Therefore, the answer depends on how many gum pads are placed in each quadrant of the mouth.
  Option A states that there are 3 gum pads in each quadrant, which makes a total of 12 gum pads.
  Option B states that there are 2 gum pads in each jaw, which makes a total of 4 gum pads.
  Option C states that there are 5 gum pads in each quadrant, which makes a total of 20 gum pads.
  Option D states that there are 2 gum pads in each quadrant, which makes a total of 8 gum pads.
  The most logical option, based on typical treatment methods, would be option A.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Thought:
  The patient had a myocardial infarction and the lipid profile showed high TG, low HDL and borderline high LDL
  The patient needs medication to lower the cholesterol and to raise the HDL levels
  Statins (Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin) are commonly used to lower cholesterol
  Fenofibrate is a fibrate that lowers triglycerides and raises HDL cholesterol
  Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate can address both high LDL and high TG, while also potentially raising HDL, making it the most appropriate choice.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  This patient had a myocardial infarction two weeks back.
  The lipid profile reveals low HDL and high LDL and TG levels, which are risk factors for further cardiovascular disease.
  Statins are first-line drugs for lowering LDL cholesterol levels.
  In this patient, additional therapy may be necessary to address the high TG levels and low HDL levels.
  Therefore, combination therapy with a fenofibrate and a statin (such as rosuvastatin) may be preferred.
  Choice A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate appears to be the preferred option.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  The patient had a recent myocardial infarction.
  The lipid profile report shows that the patient has a very high level of triglycerides, LDL and low levels of HDL.
  Statins are a class of drugs that reduce cholesterol levels in the blood.
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that lowers triglyceride levels.
  Both statins and fibric acid derivatives have been shown to reduce the risk of cardiovascular events like a myocardial infarction. 
  However, concurrent use of fibrates with statins can increase the risk of muscle injury.
  Therefore, for the given patient, the preferred treatment option would be to prescribe Rosuvastatin only as it is a potent statin and more beneficial in reducing cardiovascular risk.
  So, the answer is C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg.
Action: Answer("C")

  Rosuvastatin and atorvastatin are HMG-CoA reductase inhibitors that are used to lower cholesterol level, reduce major cardiovascular disease events and all-cause mortality.
  Given the patient's lipid profile, we need to choose a medication that will reduce triglyceride level and increase HDL level, as well as lower cholesterol level.
  Therefore, the best option would be A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought:
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by a few important structures and structures that pass through it.
  The optic stalk is the structure that connects the optic nerve to the hypothalamus and is present in the floor of the third ventricle.
  The third nerve or oculomotor nerve arises from the midbrain and passes through the lateral wall of the third ventricle.
  The infundibulum connects the pituitary gland to the hypothalamus and is also present in the floor of the third ventricle.
  The mammillary bodies are two small round bodies present on the underside of the brain posterior to the hypothalamus, but not a part of the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Mammillary body.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The structures mentioned in the options are part of the floor of third ventricle in the brain.
  Optic stalk and the infundibulum are located close to the midline and are present on the base of the third ventricle.
  Third nerve is also known as oculomotor nerve. It consists of a motor nucleus and other associated structures located in the midbrain.
  Mammillary body forms a swelling on the inferior surface of the brain and can be seen on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, all structures mentioned in the options are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("None of the above")
Response 2:
Thought:
  The third ventricle is located in the brain.
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by the hypothalamus.
  Optic stalk and Infundibulum are the structures present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  The third nerve leaves the brain and does not pass through the third ventricle.
  Mammillary bodies are located posterior to the cerebral peduncles, just inferior to the hypothalamus.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present in the floor of the third ventricle is the Third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  The floor of the third ventricle has several structures that include the optic stalks, the infundibulum, the mammillary bodies, and other structures.
  The third nerve or oculomotor nerve is present on the floor of the midbrain, and provides innervation of the eyeball and the upper and lower lids, as well as most of the extraocular muscles.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Third Nerve.
Action: Answer("B")

Response 9:
Thought:
  The third ventricle is a narrow median cleft in the diencephalon between the two thalami.
  It communicates with the left and right lateral ventricles through the interventricular foramen.
  The floor of the third ventricle includes several structures:
    - The optic chiasm, which is formed by decussation of the optic nerves
    - The infundibulum, which connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland
    - The mammillary bodies, which are important for memory
    - The tuber cinereum, which is a small eminence of gray matter in the floor of the third ventricle
    - The posterior perforated substance, which is a region of gray matter filled with numerous small blood vessels and perforations for the passage of cranial nerves and branches of the posterior cerebral artery.
  The third nerve (oculomotor nerve) emerges from the anterior aspect of the midbrain and courses around the cerebral peduncle to the lateral wall of the cavernous sinus.
  Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of the third ventricle is the third nerve.
  The answer is B: Third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")

Topic: Microbiology
Question: For which of the following is PPV-23 is most beneficial:
Choices:
  A: Cystic fibrosis patient
  B: Sickle cell anemia patient
  C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis
  D: Child less than 2 years
Response 0:
Thought: 
  PPV-23 is Pneumococcal Polysaccharide Vaccine, used for the prevention of Streptococcus pneumoniae infections.
  Cystic fibrosis patients are more susceptible to bacterial infections in the lungs.
  Sickle cell anemia is a red blood cell disorder that inhibits oxygen from reaching tissues properly, which may lead to a higher risk of infections.
  Rhinitis is inflammation of the mucous membrane of the nose, and sinusitis is sinus inflammation. Patients with these conditions have an increased risk of sinus infections that may lead to pneumonia.
  Vaccines are important for children under 2 years because they are at higher risk of developing pneumococcal infections.
  Therefore, a patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis is most beneficial for PPV-23 vaccine.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a vaccine to prevent pneumococcal disease.
  Patients with disrupted immune function are more susceptible to this infection.
  Cystic Fibrosis and Sickle cell patients have a high risk of respiratory infections due to their immune system.
  PPV-23 may increase their immune system's response to pneumococcal disease and thus be more beneficial to them.
  Sinusitis is not caused by pneumococcal disease so the vaccine may not be the best product for a patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.
  For children under 2 years, PCV13 is recommended rather than PPV-23.
  
Action: Answer("A") 

Therefore, based on the above reasoning, the most appropriate option would be A: Cystic fibrosis patient.
Response 2:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is a vaccine that protects against 23 different strains of pneumococcal bacteria.
  Patients with medical conditions affecting the immune system or respiratory system are at higher risk of developing severe infections with these bacteria.
  Patients with cystic fibrosis have lung damage which increases their risk for respiratory infections. Hence, they and the patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are more likely to benefit from the vaccine.
  Sickle cell anemia patients and children less than 2 years are at increased risk for pneumococcal infections as well. However, compared to recurrent infections caused by cystic fibrosis or rhinitis and sinusitis, their chances of vaccine benefits are less.
  Therefore, the answer is either A: Cystic fibrosis patient or C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.
Action: Answer("A") or Answer("C") - the question could have multiple good answers.
Response 3:
Thought:
PPV-23 refers to the pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine.
The S. pneumoniae bacteria cause severe infections like pneumonia, meningitis, and sepsis, particularly in people with weakened immune systems.
People who need the PPV-23 vaccine include adults over age 65 and children under 2 years old.
Cystic fibrosis and sickle cell anemia are genetic conditions, they do not directly affect the individual's susceptibility to pneumococcal disease. 
Recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis can be caused by several bacterial pathogens, but not necessarily S. pneumoniae.
The child less than 2 years is one of the patient groups recommended for the PPV-23 vaccine. 
Therefore, the answer is D: Child less than 2 years.

Children under 2 years are not vaccinated with PPV vaccine.
Patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis would benefit with PPV23 vaccination due to Streptococcus pneumoniae being the most common bacterial cause of sinusitis.
Therefore, the answer is C: Patient with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 8:
Thought:
  PPV-23 is pneumococcal polysaccharide vaccine.
  It protects against infections caused by Streptococcus pneumoniae bacteria, which can lead to pneumonia, meningitis, and bacteremia.
  Cystic fibrosis patients, sickle cell anemia patients, and patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are at an increased risk for pneumococcal disease.
  Children under the age of 2 years are typically vaccinated with PCV13 (a different pneumonia vaccine) but PPV-23 can be beneficial in certain high-risk cases.
  Answer: PPV-23 is most beneficial for patients who are at an increased risk of pneumococcal disease such as cystic fibrosis patients, sickle cell anemia patients, and patients with recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis.
  The answer is A, B and C.

### Exam: medmcqa-dev-100 | Temperature: 10.0 | Problem 17 of 100 ###
Topic: Pediatrics
Question: Short child with low T4 and raised TSH and swelling of pituitary, what is the diangosis ?
Choices:
  A: Primary hypothyrodism
  B: Pituitary tumor
  C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma
  D: TSH resistance
Response 0:
Thought: 
  T4 is thyroid hormone, and TSH is thyroid stimulating hormone
  Low thyroid hormone and high TSH indicate primary hypothyroidism or secondary hypothyroidism
  Swelling of the pituitary and raised TSH suggest a problem in the pituitary gland
  TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma is the most common cause of hyperthyroidism (not hypothyroidism) due to pituitary problems
  A pituitary tumor can compress the cells that make TSH, leading to low thyroid hormone
  Based on the symptoms described, pituitary tumor is the most likely diagnosis
  Therefore, the answer is B: Pituitary tumor
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The pituitary gland produces thyroid-stimulating hormone (TSH) which triggers the release of thyroid hormones from the thyroid gland.
  Low T4 and raised TSH levels indicate hypothyroidism, which could be due to primary hypothyroidism or secondary hypothyroidism caused by a pituitary gland problem.
  Since the patient has swelling of the pituitary, this indicates that the primary problem is related to the pituitary gland.
  A pituitary tumor or pituitary adenoma can cause an increase in TSH levels, leading to primary hypothyroidism and a low T4 level.
  Therefore, the diagnosis is C: TSH secreting pituitary adenoma.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
A short child with a low T4 level and raised TSH levels would be suggestive of hypothyroidism. 
Swelling of the pituitary gland could indicate a pituitary tumor.
A tumor of pituitary gland causing an increase in TSH secretion could suggest a TSH secreting pituitary adenoma.
Therefore, the most likely diagnosis is C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  The child is short, has low T4 and high TSH, and swelling of the pituitary gland. 
  Primary hypothyroidism is characterized by high TSH and low T4 levels, but pituitary swelling is not a feature of it. 
  A pituitary tumor may present with high TSH levels, but it would not cause low T4 levels. 
  TSH resistance may present with high TSH levels but not low T4 levels, and pituitary swelling is not a feature of it. 
  TSH-secreting pituitary adenoma presents with high TSH and normal or high T4 levels, and pituitary swelling is a characteristic finding. 
  Therefore, the diagnosis is C: TSH secreting pituitary adenoma. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 4:
Thought: 
  T4 is thyroxine which is a hormone secreted by the thyroid gland.
  TSH is a hormone secreted by the pituitary gland.
  In primary hypothyroidism, T4 is low and TSH is raised.
  But in this case, both T4 is low and TSH is raised, so the patient has secondary hypothyroidism.
  The swelling of the pituitary also indicates a pituitary adenoma.
  The diagnosis for this clinical presentation is TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma.
  The answer is C: TSH Secreting pituitary adenoma.

- Chemical bonding helps to create a strong bond between the tooth's surface and the dental material
- Composites are often used for restoration, but they do not chemical bond with enamel
- Polycarboxylate cements provide an adhesive layer to the tooth surface, but they don't form a chemical bond with enamel
- BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants provide a chemical bond with enamel.
- Therefore, the answer is D: BIS-GMA resins in pit and fissure sealants

Thought:
  Chemical bond with enamel is necessary for long-term adhesion.
  Composites, direct filling resins, and pit and fissure sealants are restorative materials which are used to repair or prevent dental caries.

Topic: Surgery
Question: Which one of the following is a muscle splitting incision?
Choices:
  A: Kocher's incision
  B: Rutherford-Morrison incision
  C: Pfannenstiel incision
  D: Lanz incision
Response 0:
Thought: 
Muscle splitting incisions are a type of incision that divides the muscle fibers parallel to the muscle bundles.
Kocher's incision, Lanz incision, and Rutherford-Morrison incisions are vertical incisions used to access the abdominal cavity, gallbladder, and kidney, respectively. 
Pfannenstiel incision is a transverse incision made just above the pubic symphysis and below the anterior superior iliac spine.
Therefore, the answer is C: Pfannenstiel incision
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
Muscle splitting incision is the one that avoids going through the muscles themselves. Kocher's incision is often used during an appendectomy, and it goes between the external oblique muscle and the lateral margin of the rectus muscle. Rutherford-Morrison incision is used commonly in emergency appendectomy as well and it goes over the right iliac fossa. Pfannenstiel incision is a transverse incision made in the lower abdomen, generally below the navel, useful for operations such as a C-section. Lanz incision is a transverse incision that follows the Langer's line of the abdomen and its often used for surgeries on lower abdomen such as appendectomy.
Therefore, the only one of the options that seems to be a muscle splitting incision is Kocher's incision.
Action: Answer("A")

Thought:

    Pfannenstiel incision is made in the lower abdomen to gain access to pelvic organs. It is a transverse incision and not a muscle splitting incision.
    Kocher's incision is an oblique incision that starts from the midpoint of the inguinal ligament, goes to the anterior superior iliac spine and then to the pubic crest. It provides access to the hip joint.
    Rutherford-Morrison incision is another name for paramedian incision which is a linear midline incision through the linea alba. It is not a muscle splitting incision.
    Lanz incision is also known as gridiron incision. It is made in the right lower quadrant of the abdomen and it is not a muscle splitting incision.
    Therefore, the answer is not A, C or D.

  Mitis salivarius bacitracin agar (MSB) has a pH indicator, which makes colonies appear as blue or green, while inhibiting growth of other streptococcal species that are also found in oral flora.
  Therefore, the most used selective medium for Streptococcus rnutans is B: Mitus salivarius bacitracin agar.
Action: Answer("B")

Choices:
  A: Long teeth
  B: Short teeth
  C: Tipped teeth
  D: Tapered teeth

  The ideal tooth for a PVC is the one that is simply missing a small part of the tooth.
  Tapered teeth with small or no occlusal space for the crown are contraindicated for PVC.
  Teeth with some degree of tipping contact of adjacent teeth may receive PVC but those that are severely tipped may be contraindicated for PVC.
  Short teeth would need a full veneer crown and Long teeth would require reduction.
  Therefore, PVCs are contraindicated for tapered teeth.

  Short teeth, Tipped teeth or Tapered teeth are not contraindicated in partial veneer crown.

Topic: Pathology
Question: Naive T cell get activated by:
Choices:
  A: NK cell
  B: Dendritic cell
  C: Macrophage
  D: B-lymphocyte
Response 0:
Thought:
Naive T cells are activated by Antigen-Presenting Cells (APCs).
Among APCs, dendritic cells are the most potent activators of naive T cells.
Therefore, the answer is B: Dendritic cell.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Naive T cells express T cell receptors (TCRs).
  The TCRs on Naive T cells are specific for one type of antigen.
  Naive T cells can be activated by professional antigen-presenting cells (pAPCs), such as dendritic cells, macrophages, and B cells.
  These pAPCs present processed antigens to naive T cells in the context of MHC molecules.
  Natural killer (NK) cells, in contrast, recognize stress-induced molecules on target cells via NK activating receptors.
  Therefore, naive T cell get activated by professional antigen-presenting cells (pAPCs), such as dendritic cells, macrophages, and B cells.
  The answer is B: Dendritic cell.

Choices:

  B: NADPH oxidase
  C: Superoxide dismutase
  D: Catalase

  Reactive oxygen metabolites are toxic compounds.
  Lysosomes are subcellular organelles involved in intracellular digestion.
  Peroxidase and NADPH oxidase are not usually found in lysosomes.
  Superoxide dismutase is an enzyme that is found in the cytoplasm but not lysosomes.
  Catalase is a lysosomal enzyme involved in the scavenging of excess H2O2
  Therefore, the correct answer is D: Catalase.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Lysosomes contain enzymes that can break down cellular waste and debris.
  Reactive oxygen metabolites are generated by lysosomal enzymes.
  Peroxidase is not specific to lysosomes, and is not directly involved in the generation of reactive oxygen species by lysosomes.
  NADPH oxidase generates reactive oxygen species outside of lysosomes, usually in phagocytes.
  Superoxide dismutase inactivates superoxide anions which are oxygen radicals generated during aerobic metabolism.
  Catalase is found in peroxisomes and is involved in the breakdown of hydrogen peroxide.
  Therefore, none of the enzymes listed are directly responsible for the release of reactive oxygen metabolites in lysosomes.

  Therefore, the enzyme that releases reactive oxygen metabolite in lysosomes is NADPH oxidase.

 Catalase converts hydrogen peroxide to water and oxygen.

  The tensor veli palatine (tensor palatini) is innervated by the medial pterygoid nerve, which is a branch of the mandibular division of the trigeminal nerve (V3).

- Auditory pathway is the sensory pathway for sound.
- It starts from the ear and ends up to the brainstem and ultimately to the auditory cortex.
- Cochlear Nucleus is the first order nucleus for auditory information in the brainstem, after the hair cells in the cochlea
- The cochlear nucleus receives the auditory information through the auditory nerve fibers, then it projects to the superior olivary complex (SOC)
- The SOC projects to the inferior colliculus (IC)
- The IC processes and integrates the information from both ears and sends outputs to the medial geniculate body (MGB) via the lateral lemniscus.
- The MGB then relays the auditory information to the auditory cortex via the auditory radiations.
- Thus, the correct sequence of auditory pathway from peripheral to central is B>C>A>D.
- Therefore, the answer is B: B>D>C>A.

Question: Working cusps are also known as:
Choices:
  A: Guiding cusps.
  B: Supporting cusps.
  C: Holding cusps.
  D: Balancing cusps.
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Working cusps are those cusps on the maxillary and mandibular teeth that are involved in mastication or biting.
  Guiding cusps are a non-working cusp that touches an opposing tooth during excursive movement.
  Balancing cusps are non-working cusps in the opposite arch that contact each other during lateral jaw movement.
  Supporting cusps is not a term commonly used in dentistry.
  Holding cusps is not a term commonly used in dentistry.
  Therefore, the working cusps are also known as Guiding cusps.
Action: Answer("A")

  Holding cusps seems unlikely.
  Balancing cusps guide the remaining movement of the mandible in lateral, protrusive and retrusive movements.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Guiding cusps.

Question: Most common route for metastasis of oral cancer is by:
Choices:
  A: Direct extension
  B: Lymphatics
  C: Blood vessels
  D: Aspiration of tumor cells
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The most common route for metastasis of oral cancer is through the lymphatics, which are the channels that carry lymph (a fluid containing white blood cells) throughout the body.
  Direct extension refers to the invasion of tumor cells into neighboring tissues.
  Blood vessels are not usually the primary route of metastasis in oral cancer.
  Aspiration of tumor cells is not a common route for metastasis either.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Lymphatics.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought: 
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure done in dental treatment.
  Root denudation is a problem where the tooth's root is exposed, and the gum line recedes.
  PDL fibres attach to the cementum of the tooth's root.
  In the case of roots denuded for six years, the cementum can become damaged or may not exist.
  If the cementum is damaged or nonexistent, the PDL fibres may start connecting to the dentin.
  Root denudation can cause changes in epithelial cells and tissues.
  Therefore, the answer is B: PDL fibres attached to dentin.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
A lateral sliding flap is a surgical technique where a flap is raised on one side of the tooth and slid over the adjacent area before being repositioned to cover the bone again.
The PDL fibers are responsible to attach cementum to alveolar bone.
Since the tooth roots have been denuded for 6 years, the PDL fibers will not be present and those being connected will not be possible.
The dental tissue remaining after denudation will be dentin and not cementum.
Epithelial tissue would not be present as it does not attach to the root surface.
The co-adaptation to the remaining fibers is a possible result if remaining PDL fibers are abundant.
Therefore, the most appropriate answer to this question is D: Co-adaptation to the remaining fibers. 

Action: Answer("D")

  Epithelium will not attach to a previously denuded surface and will tend to form long junctional epithelium.
  Co adaptation of remaining fibers is incorrect because the previous statement suggests that the periodontal ligament is damaged.
  Therefore, since the periodontal ligament fibers are likely to be reabsorbed, the lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years would show epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.

Topic: Biochemistry
Question: Which of the following has least density?
Choices:
  A: VLDL
  B: LDL
  C: HDL
  D: Chylomicrons
Response 0:
Thought:
- All of these types of lipoproteins are made of protein and lipids
- VLDL (Very Low Density Lipoprotein) is the largest of the four types of lipoproteins and is made mostly of triglycerides
- LDL (Low Density Lipoprotein) is often referred to as bad cholesterol. It is smaller than VLDL and has slightly more protein in it.
- HDL (High Density Lipoprotein) is often referred to as good cholesterol. It is the smallest and densest of the four types of lipoproteins, and made up mostly of protein.
- Chylomicrons are made up mostly of triglycerides and are the largest of the lipoproteins.
- Therefore, HDL has least density because it is smallest and most dense.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  All of the given options contain lipoproteins.
  Lipoproteins are complexes of lipids and proteins.
  Chylomicrons contains the highest percentage of lipids among all lipoproteins.
  Among the remaining options, VLDL is the least dense. 
  Therefore, the answer is A: VLDL.

  Chylomicrons > VLDL > LDL > HDL.

Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?

  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Thought:
  The Bishop Score is used to predict whether a woman will have a successful induction of labor.
  The score is calculated by adding points based on dilation, effacement, consistency, position, and fetal station.
  Dilation: 1 cm is scored as 0.
  Effacement: 30% is scored as 0.
  Fetal station: -1 station is scored as 0.
  Cervical consistency: Soft is scored as 1.
  Cervical position: Posterior is scored as 0.
  Therefore, the total modified Bishop score would be 1.
  The answer is not listed as one of the choices, Therefore, the closest answer is B: 3, which is the Bishop score if the patient had 2 cm dilation, 50% effacement, -2 station, cervix is firm and middle.

  The components of the Bishop Score are cervical dilation, cervical effacement, cervical consistency, fetal station, and fetal position.
  The scores of the five components are added to determine the total Bishop Score.
  The Bishop Score ranges from 0 to 13, and a score of more than 8 is associated with a high likelihood of successful vaginal delivery.
  In this question, the woman is 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor.
  On per vaginal examination: 
    1 cm dilation is assigned a score of 0
    30% effacement is assigned a score of 0
    soft and posterior cervix is assigned a score of 1
    veex at --1 station is assigned a score of 0
  Therefore, the Modified Bishop Score is 1+0+1+0=2
  The answer is not in the options, but the correct value of modified bishop score is 2.

Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:

  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Thought:
- Malocclusion refers to the misalignment of teeth.
- Prevalence rate is the total number of cases of a particular disease or health condition in a population during a specific period.
- Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a particular disease or health condition that develop in a population during a specific period.
- Morbidity refers to the incidence of disease, sickness, and disability in a population.
- Probability refers to the likelihood or chance of an event occurring.
- Since the question is asking about the occurrence of malocclusion in a given population, the best choice to describe it is prevalence rate.
Action: Answer("A")

  Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a disease or condition in a population within a specific time period. It tells us how quickly the population is developing new cases of the disease or condition.
  Morbidity refers to the burden of a disease or condition, including both the incidence and the duration of the disease or condition.
  Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring.
  Since malocclusion is a condition and the question is asking for the best description of the frequency of the condition in the population, we should choose a term that fits with the characteristics of a condition or disease.
  Prevalence rate is the most appropriate choice here because it describes how widespread malocclusion is in the population.

Question: Best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is :
Choices:
  A: L:S ratio
  B: Lecithin-cephalin ratio
  C: Phosphatidyl choline
  D: Phosphatidyl glycerol
Response 0:
Thought:
  A diabetic mother is at a risk of delivering a preterm baby.
  L:S ratio and Lecithin-cephalin ratio are tests done to evaluate fetal lung maturity.
  Phosphatidylglycerol and phosphatidylcholine are special lipids found in fetal alveoli surfactant.
  Phosphatidylglycerol is the best test for fetal lung maturity in a diabetic mother.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Diabetic pregnancies tend to be at risk for premature delivery.
  Lung maturity testing is used to determine fetal readiness for delivery.
  Phosphatidylglycerol is detectable late in the second trimester or early in third trimester, and its presence has been associated with fetal lung maturity.
  Thus, the best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is testing for Phosphatidylglycerol.
  The answer is D: Phosphatidyl glycerol.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought:

  Therefore, the best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is D: Phosphatidyl glycerol.

  Phosphatidyl choline is not a commonly used test for fetal lung maturity.
  Phosphatidyl glycerol (PG) test has high sensitivity and specificity in predicting fetal lung maturity and is the best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother.
   
Action: Answer("D")
Response 9:
Thought: 
  Since diabetic mothers are at higher risk, determining fetal maturity is important to prevent complications during delivery.
  L:S ratio, Lecithin-cephalin ratio, Phosphatidyl choline, and Phosphatidyl glycerol are all possible tests used in determining fetal lung maturity.
  L:S ratio and Lecithin-cephalin ratio are used to predict the risk of respiratory distress syndrome (RDS).
  Phosphatidyl choline is used to evaluate lung maturity, but is less sensitive than Phosphatidyl glycerol.
  Phosphatidyl glycerol is present in amniotic fluid only after 35 weeks of gestation, and is a highly sensitive marker for fetal lung maturity.
  Therefore, the best test for fetal maturity in a diabetic mother is D: Phosphatidyl glycerol.

Topic: Pathology
Question: Iron entry into enterocytes occurs which of the following?
Choices:
  A: DMT-1
  B: Ferropoin
  C: Transferrin
  D: Hepcidin
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Iron absorption occurs in the proximal small intestine, specifically in the duodenum.
  Enterocytes are the cells lining the small intestine.
  Iron absorption requires a transporter at the brush border membrane in the enterocytes.
  The DMT-1 transporter is responsible for the uptake of iron.
  Ferropoin does not play a role in the iron entry into enterocytes.
  Transferrin is an iron transport protein in the blood and not found in enterocytes.
  Hepcidin is an iron regulatory hormone that inhibits iron absorption.
  Therefore, the correct answer is A: DMT-1.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Iron entry into enterocytes occur through two transporters; DMT-1 and Ferroportin.
    DMT-1 is expressed on the apical membrane of duodenal enterocytes and mediates uptake of ferrous iron from the gut lumen into epithelial cells. 
    Ferroportin 1 is expressed on the basolateral membrane of enterocytes, it exports iron from the enterocyte into the circulation.
  Transferrin is not involved in Iron uptake into enterocytes. It is a plasma protein that binds to iron and carries it to the liver and other tissues for storage.
  Hepcidin is a hormone synthesized in the liver that regulates the iron homeostasis which inhibits the action of ferroportin.
  Therefore, the answer is A: DMT-1 and B: Ferropoin.
  
Action: Answer("A and B")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Iron is an essential element in the body, it has to be taken up in order to be utilized by the body. 
  Enterocytes are specialized absorptive cells in the small intestine. 
  Iron enters these cells mainly through divalent metal transporter-1 (DMT-1) 
  Ferropoin is a fictional element.
  Transferrin is a carrier protein that binds to iron and transports it in the blood.
  Hepcidin is a hormone that regulates iron metabolism.
  Therefore, the answer is A: DMT-1.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 3:
Thought:
Iron entry into enterocytes occurs via DMT-1 (divalent metal transporter 1), which is a transmembrane protein found in the duodenum and proximal jejunum of the small intestine.
Ferropoin is a fictional term.
Transferrin is a serum protein which serves as a transporter of iron throughout the body.
Hepcidin is a hormone produced by the liver that plays a key role in regulating iron metabolism in the body; however, it is not involved in the process of iron entry into enterocytes.
Therefore, the answer is A: DMT-1.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 4:
Thought: 
  Iron entry into enterocytes refers to the process of transporting iron from the lumen of small intestine across the enterocyte and into the circulation.
  DMT-1 (divalent metal transporter-1) mediates the transport of dietary non-heme iron across the apical membrane of intestinal enterocyte.
  Ferroportin is the only known iron exporter protein in mammalian cells. It mediates the export of cellular iron across the basolateral membranes of the enterocytes and into the circulation.
  Transferrin is a blood plasma protein that binds iron molecules and transports iron from the intestine, reticuloendothelial system, and liver to all proliferating cells in the body.
  Hepcidin is a hormone produced by the liver which helps to regulate iron metabolism by controlling the rate of iron absorption by the intestines and the amount of iron the body can recycle from old red blood cells.
  Therefore, Answer is A: DMT-1

  Iron is required for the synthesis of heme.
  Humans absorb iron as heme (from meat) or ferric and ferrous iron.

  DMT-1 (divalent metal transporter-1) is responsible for the transport of ferrous iron across the brush border membrane of enterocytes.
  Hephaestin, a copper-containing oxidase that is bound to the basolateral membrane, oxidizes the ferrous iron to the ferric (Fe3+) form.
  Transferrin and Ferropoin are not involved in the enterocytes' iron transport.

  Hepcidin, a peptide hormone synthesized by the liver, regulates iron homeostasis by binding ferroportin causing its internalization and degradation.
  Therefore, iron entry into enterocytes occurs mainly via two mechanisms, endocytosis of circulating iron-bound transferrin and transmembrane transport via DMT-1.

Topic: Dental
Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummer’s classification
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Multi-constricted apical constriction refers to having two or more points of constriction at the root apex of the tooth.
  The Dummer's classification is used to classify the number of roots and root canals in a tooth.
  Type 1 has a single canal and a single apex.
  Type 2 typically has one main canal with one or two lateral canals and a single apex.
  Type 3 has three or more canals and has a maximum of three separate apical foramina.
  Type 4 typically has four or more canals and can have four or more separate apical foramina.
  Based on this, multi-constricted apical constriction would most likely be seen in a tooth with multiple canals or in type 4 of Dummer's classification.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is used to categorize root canal systems of molars.
  Multi constricted apical constriction defines a Level 1 canal configuration.
  In Dummer's classification, Type 1 represents a single canal in each root.
  Type 2 represents two separate canals of which one in each root will open separately into the pulp chamber.
  Type 3 represents two canals in one root and one canal in each of the remaining roots.
  Type 4 represents two canals in each root.
  Based on these facts, multi constricted apical constriction is only seen in Type 4 canals.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("D")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Dummer’s classification is a classification system for root canal morphology.
  Multi constricted apical constriction refers to the presence of several small constrictions at the apical portion of the root canal.
  In Dummer’s classification, Type 4 indicates that there is more than one apical canal with separate foramina through which they exit.
  If there is multi constricted apical constriction, it means that there is only one canal, but it has multiple small constrictions near the apex.
  This is classified as Type 2 in Dummer’s classification.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 3:
Thought: 
  Dummer’s classification is a classification system used in endodontics to observe root canal anatomy.
  Multi constricted apical constriction is a feature of root canals that exhibit accessory canals and multiple apical foramina.
  Type 1 of Dummer's classification is for root canals with a single apical foramen or narrow oval shape.
  Type 2 of Dummer's classification is for root canals with a single apical foramen but wider oval shape.
  Type 3 of Dummer's classification is for root canals with multiple apical foramina present on the same side of the root orifice.
  Type 4 of Dummer's classification is for root canals with multiple apical foramina present on both sides of the root orifice.
  Therefore, since multi constricted apical constriction is a feature of root canals with multiple apical foramina, it is seen in Dummer's classification Type 3 and Type 4.
  The answer is either C: Type 3 or D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("C") or Answer("D")

  The apical constriction is a narrow zone at the apical end of the root canal system.

  According to Dummer's classification:
  - Type 1 canal has one main canal with no branches.
  - Type 2 canal has one main canal with branches.
  - Type 3 canal has two or more separate and distinct canals.
  - Type 4 canal has one main canal that divides into two separate and distinct branches.
  Multi-constricted apical constriction means there are multiple narrow zones at the apical end of the root canal system.
  Based on the description, it is most likely to be found in Type 4 canals, which have multiple branches.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.

  Type 3 is a tooth with two canals.

  Multi-constricted apical constriction is most likely seen in teeth with multiple canals.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought: 
Multi constricted apical constriction is a term used for teeth where the apical constriction is seen with multiple splits.
Dummer's classification is based on the complexity of the root canal system.
 Type 1 has a single canal from the pulp chamber to the apex of the tooth.
 Type 2 has two canals that join together before the apex.
 Type 3 has one main canal but with extra tiny canals in the pulp chamber.
 Type 4 has two separate and distinct canals with separate apical foramina, and also an extra accessory canal.
Since "multi constricted apical constriction" is not the characteristic usually mentioned in other types, so I believe it could be Type 4 which has accessory canal as its characteristic.
Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.

Question: The primary site of action of antidiuretic hormone is on the:
Choices:
  A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney
  B: Afferent arterioles of the glomeruli
  C: Thirst center in the hypothalamus
  D: Osmoreceptors in the hypothalamus
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Antidiuretic hormone (ADH) is also known as vasopressin and is synthesized in the hypothalamus.
  It regulates water balance in the body.
  ADH acts on the collecting ducts of the kidney and increases water reabsorption.
  Therefore, the primary site of action of antidiuretic hormone is on the distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
Antidiuretic hormone (ADH) is also known as vasopressin.
ADH is synthesized in the hypothalamus and is transported to the posterior pituitary gland, where it is stored and released in response to an increase in blood osmolality.
ADH acts on the kidneys to promote water reabsorption by increasing the permeability of the distal tubules and collecting ducts to water.
Therefore, the primary site of action of antidiuretic hormone is the distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.
The answer is A: Distal tubules and collecting ducts in the kidney.

  In this case, the patient has recurrent gingival swelling and pain in teeth 61 and 62, which are primary maxillary anterior teeth.
  Treatment will depend on the severity of the decay and the extent of gingival involvement.
  Extraction and endodontic treatment may not be appropriate given the patient's age and stage of development.
  Restoration may be a viable option, but fluoride application (topical or systemic) combined with behavioral modifications addressing diet and hygiene are important interventions in managing S-ECC at early stages.
  Therefore, the line of treatment will be D: Fluoride application.

Topic: Dental
Question: Object permanence seen in which stage of Jean Piaget’s theory
Choices:
  A: Sensorimotor
  B: Pre-operational stage
  C: Concrete operations stage
  D: Formal operations stage
Response 0:
Thought:
  Object permanence is the understanding that an object continues to exist even if it is not seen or touched.
  Jean Piaget's theory studies stages of cognitive development.
  The Sensorimotor stage is from birth to 2 years old, and object permanence happens at this age.
  Therefore, Object permanence is seen in the Sensorimotor stage of Jean Piaget's theory. 
  The answer is A: Sensorimotor.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Jean Piaget's theory of cognitive development includes four stages:
  1. Sensorimotor
  2. Pre-operational
  3. Concrete operations
  4. Formal operations
  Object permanence refers to the ability to understand that an object still exists even if it is no longer visible. 
  Object permanence develops in infants in the first 2 years of life.
  Therefore, the stage of Jean Piaget's theory in which object permanence is seen is the Sensorimotor stage.
  The answer is A: Sensorimotor.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Object permanence is the understanding that objects do not cease to exist when they are hidden from our view. 
  According to Jean Piaget's theory, this understanding is acquired by infants around 8 months old.
  The stage of development associated with this understanding is the Sensorimotor stage, which occurs from birth to around 2 years old.
  The Pre-operational stage occurs from ages 2 to 7, in which children develop symbolic thinking but do not yet understand abstract concepts like time or cause and effect.
  The Concrete operations stage happens from ages 7 to 11, where the child becomes less egocentric, understands conservation, hierarchical classification, and understands the concept of reversibility.
  The Formal operations stage occurs from age 12 onwards, where the individual becomes capable of hypothetical and deductive reasoning.
  Therefore, object permanence is seen in the Sensorimotor stage of Jean Piaget’s theory.

  B: Helsinki declaration
  C: Hippocratic oath

  Biomedical research in human subjects should follow ethical principles that protect the rights and safety of those subjects.

  The Geneva Declaration and the International Code of Medical Ethics have provisions related to the conduct of research; however, they do not specifically address research in human subjects. 
  The Hippocratic oath is an ancient ethical code that governs the behavior of medical professionals. 
  The Helsinki Declaration, developed by the World Medical Association, specifically governs biomedical research in human subjects. It provides guidelines for researchers to ensure that research is conducted with respect for the dignity, rights, and safety of the research subjects. 
  Therefore, the answer is B: Helsinki declaration.

Topic: Physiology
Question: Which of the following is rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles is?
Choices:
  A: Glycolysis
  B: Glycogenolysis
  C: TCA cycle
  D: Phosphocreatine
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Rapid source of energy means anaerobic pathway.
  Glycolysis is an anaerobic process that breaks down glucose to pyruvate and resynthesizes ATP.
  Glycogenolysis is breakdown of glycogen into glucose, and then glucose enters glycolysis to resynthesize ATP.
  TCA cycle is responsible for metabolic breakdown of carbohydrates and fatty acids, generating ATP and releasing carbon dioxide.
  Phosphocreatine is a high-energy phosphate molecule that can be rapidly broken down to resynthesize ATP.
  Therefore, the fastest source of ATP resynthesis is Phosphocreatine.
Answer: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Thought: 
- When muscles need energy, ATP is broken down into ADP and Pi, which releases energy used for muscle contraction.
- Phosphocreatine is a high-energy molecule stored in muscles that can quickly donate a phosphate group to ADP to resynthesize ATP for muscle contraction.
- Therefore, the rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles is phosphocreatine.
- The answer is D: Phosphocreatine.

Question: What is the level of proteinuria to diagnose severe preeclampsia?
Choices:
  A: 20 mg
  B: 200 mg
  C: 300 mg
  D: 3000 mg
Response 0:

  Preeclampsia is a serious pregnancy condition characterized by high blood pressure and damage to organs such as liver and kidneys.

  D: Type 4

Thought:
  In root canal anatomy, C-shaped canals are shaped like a C, and there are four types of them according to Melton and Seitzor classification.
  Knowing that one of these types of canals is semi-colon shaped and C-shaped, we can determine the classification of this type of canal.

Action: Answer("C") 

Therefore, the semi colon shaped C shaped canal is classified as C: Type 3.
Response 1:
Thought:
  Melton and Seitzor's classification of C-shaped canal is based on the number of canals and the configuration of the canal anatomy.
  Type 1 is a single canal, type 2 is two separate canals, and type 3 is two canals that join into a single canal.
  A type 4 configuration is extremely complex and unusual.
  A semicolon-shaped C-shaped canal would be a type 3 since it is a single canal formed by the joining of two smaller canals.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  According to Melton and Seitzor, there are four classifications for C-shaped canals.
  Type 1 - the canal is deeply buried in the dentine and looks like a fusion of two canals.
  Type 2 - the canal is a thin C shape, often with clear pulp tissue down the main canal and another one in the lateral canals.
  Type 3 - the canal is a thick C shape, with pulp over the entire circumference of the canal.
  Type 4 - the canal is not present throughout the entire root length.
  Given that the canal in question is described as "semi colon shaped C shaped canal," it is likely a Type 2 C-shaped canal.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Type 2.

Topic: Pharmacology
Question: Which of the following instructions should be given to a lactating mother regarding drug usage?
Choices:
  A: No advice is required as most of the drugs are secreted negligibly in the milk
  B: Take drugs with longer half-life
  C: Tell her to feed the baby just before next dose
  D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug
Response 0:
Thought:
  Drugs can pass into breast milk and can affect the baby. 
  The safety of any drug during breastfeeding depends on its plasma concentration, lipid solubility, molecular weight, and protein binding.
  The best course of action is to avoid the use of medication while breastfeeding if possible.
  If a medication is necessary, the lowest effective dose of a drug with the shortest half-life should be used.
  Instructions are required for drug usage in lactating mothers.
  Options A, B, and D do not provide safe instructions.
  Therefore, the most appropriate option is C, as feeding a baby just before the next drug dose is due can reduce the amount of drug in the milk. 
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  Lactating mothers require special considerations while taking medications.
  Drugs can be secreted in milk and may affect the baby.
  Most of the drugs have some concentration in milk.
  Choices A and B are incorrect because even though most of the drugs are secreted in negligible amounts in milk, some drugs can cause harm to the baby. Additionally, longer half-life drugs means the drug will stay longer in the body, increasing the chances of exposure.
  Choice C is partially correct as feeding the baby just before the next dose can reduce the concentration of drugs in milk. However, if the drug needs to be taken several times a day, this cannot be done every time.
  It is advisable to avoid drugs in the first place. However, if a drug is required, the mother should avoid breastfeeding during peak concentration or for the duration of treatment, as per advice by a medical professional.
  Therefore, the best answer is D: Do not feed the baby if you are consuming any drug.
Action: Answer("D")

Thought: 
  The question asks about drug usage and lactation.
  Some drugs can be secreted into breastmilk and could be harmful to the baby.
  It is important for lactating mothers to be careful with drug usage.
  The correct answer should reflect the best advice for a lactating mother to follow when using drugs.
  Option A is incorrect because some drugs can be secreted in breastmilk.
  Option B is incorrect because drugs with longer half-life could accumulate in breastmilk and harm the baby.
  Option C could be an option, but it is not the best advice.
  Option D is incorrect because lactating mothers should never withhold breastfeeding without consulting with a physician.
  The best answer would be to tell the lactating mother to avoid taking or minimize the dose of drugs while breastfeeding and to always seek medical advice before taking any medication.
  None of the answer choices reflect this best practice.

Thought:
- If a lactating mother consumes drugs, they can be secreted in her milk and affect the baby.
- The mother should take steps to minimize drug excretion in her milk.
- Feeding the baby just before the dose can reduce drug concentration in milk.
- Longer half-life means greater accumulation of drug in the body and milk.
- Telling the mother to not feed the baby while consuming the drug can be harmful for the baby.
- Therefore, the best option is to instruct the mother to feed the baby just before the next dose.

Lactating mothers pass on most of the drugs they consume through their milk, hence need caution while consuming the drugs.
The ideal scenario would be to suggest an alternative/non-drug therapy, especially if there are safety concerns.
If drug usage is mandatory, then the dose, duration, and route of administration should be carefully considered.
Feeding the baby just before the next dose will minimize milk drug levels during peak maternal blood drug concentration.
Hence the answer is C: Tell her to feed the baby just before the next dose.

  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought:
  In the heme biosynthetic pathway, there are multiple enzymes that utilize many substrates and intermediates.
  The inhibition of certain enzymes is a characteristic effect of Lead poisoning.
  Among the enzymes inhibited, Ferrochelatase is the last enzyme in the heme biosynthetic pathway that inserts Ferrous Iron into Protoporphyrin IX to produce Heme.
  The inhibition of earlier enzymes in the pathway would lead to the accumulation of certain intermediates.
  Inhibition of the enzyme, ALA dehydratase, the second enzyme in the pathway, leads to the accumulation of Delta-aminolevulinic acid (ALA) in blood.
  The accumulation of porphobilinogen, the substrate of PBG deaminase, and uroporphyrinogen-III, a later intermediate in the pathway can occur in acute intermittent porphyrias but not in lead poisoning.
  Therefore, the substance that accumulates in blood in lead poisoning is Delta amino levulinic acid.

Question: A rest seat is prepared as:
Choices:
  A: Spoon shaped depression with the apex towards the center of the tooth
  B: Concavity with hemisphere shape
  C: Elliptical shape
  D: Rhomboid depression limited to enamel
Response 0:
Thought: 
  A rest seat is a mechanical feature that provides vertical support for a removable prosthesis.
  The rest seat provides resistance to the dislodging forces of the denture base.
  Spoon-shaped depression is concave depression in a rest seat under one or both of the proximal plates of a removable partial denture.
  Hemisphere shape can be prepared in lingual surface of the abutment tooth.
  Elliptical shape depression under the incisal edge using a round bur.
  Rhomboid depression is prepared in the mesial or distal aspect of a tooth serving as an indirect retainer.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Spoon shaped depression with the apex towards the center of the tooth.
Action: Answer("A")

  It is used to support an indirect restoration(prosthesis).

  Therefore, the answer is A: Spoon shaped depression with the apex towards the center of the tooth.

Topic: Social & Preventive Medicine
Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Simple random sampling involves selecting study subjects randomly, without bias.
  Stratified random sampling involves dividing the population into categories, then randomly selecting subjects from each category.
  Systematic random sampling involves selecting subjects at fixed intervals in a random fashion from a sample frame.
  Cluster sampling involves randomly selecting and grouping clusters of participants.
  The question is talking about selecting patients based on potential factors that may affect results. 
  Stratified random sampling is used to reduce potential confounding factors. 
  Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
- It's not simple random sampling as it's totally random 
- It's not cluster sampling either as in Cluster sampling the sampling is done in groups.
- Stratified random sampling involves dividing the population into different subgroups, which are then sampled separately. 
- Systematic random sampling involves selecting a random starting point then picking every nth unit in succession from the sampling frame.
- The question mentions selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results, so stratified random sampling seems to fit the description. 
- Therefore, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.

Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought: 
   Systematic random sampling is selecting every 'n'th participant in a list.
   Simple random sampling is selecting the participants at a random.
   In Stratified random sampling, the population is divided into non-overlapping strata, and then a simple random sample is taken within each stratum.
   Cluster sampling involves the selection of naturally occurring groups and then randomly selecting individuals within them.
   Since we have to select the patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results, Stratified random sampling can help ensure any subgroups that may exist are represented.
   Hence, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling.

- Stratified random sampling involves dividing a population into subgroups and then randomly selecting individuals from each subgroup. This helps ensure that each subgroup is represented in the sample.
- Cluster sampling involves dividing the population into clusters, and then randomly selecting some of those clusters. This method does not match the requirements of the question.

  Stratified random sampling is a type of probability sampling in which the population is divided into strata (sub-groups) based on some characteristic and a sample is taken from each stratum.
  Cluster sampling is a type of probability sampling in which the population is divided into clusters and a simple random sample of clusters is selected, and then a sample of elements is selected from each of the chosen clusters.
  Among these options, stratified random sampling is the only one that takes into account the potential factors that will affect the results by dividing the population into sub-groups according to some characteristic of interest.

Question: A 10-year boy with dog bite unprovoked comes to you. Appropriate action is:
Choices:
  A: Give cell culture derived vaccine
  B: Withhold vaccine and observe dog for 10 days
  C: Kill dog and send brain for biopsy
  D: No fuher action is necessary
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Animal bites can cause rabies.
  Vaccination can be used as a preventive measure against rabies.
  10-year old boy with a dog bite unprovoked has a higher chance of getting rabies.
  Withholding vaccine and observing the dog for 10 days is not an appropriate action in this situation.
  Killing the dog and sending its brain for biopsy is not an appropriate action and can be considered as animal cruelty.
  Therefore, the appropriate action is to give cell culture derived vaccine.
  The answer is A: Give cell culture derived vaccine.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
 For bites by unprovoked dogs, rabies prophylaxis is required.
 Rabies prophylaxis includes:
     -Cleaning and suturing the wound
     -Administration of anti-rabies serum (ARS) + cell culture vaccine (CCV) on 0 day. 
     -CCV on days 3, 7, 14, and 28 (0.5 ml s.c.).
Since the boy has not been vaccinated previously and the dog was unprovoked, Anti-rabies serum (ARS) and cell culture vaccine should be initiated as per the schedule.
Therefore, the appropriate action is to give cell culture derived vaccine.

  Class I is normal occlusion.
  Class II is characterized by retrognathic mandible and/or a prognathic maxilla (overjet).
  There are two types of Class II: Div I (maxillary protrusion) and Div II (maxillary central incisors are upright or retruded and the laterals are protruded).
  Therefore, the answer depends on which Class II type has strong familial inheritance:
    Class II div I: Maxillary protrusion genes carries near 50% dominant rate.
  The answer is C: Class II div I.
